  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e25c763b-e746-40e9-82db-4633b5c53c89'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1304862412799914467">متزامنة مع الذكرى الستين لاحتلال فلسطين, تصدر (زمن الخيول البيضاء) رواية ملحمية استثنائية يتوج بها الشاعر والروائي إبراهيم نصرالله مشروعه الروائي الكبير ( الملهاة الفلسطينية ) الذي بدأ العمل عليه منذ عام 1985 , و الذي صدر منه ست روايات لكل رواية أجواؤها الخاصة بهاو شخوصها و بناؤها الفني و استقلالها عن الروايات الأخرى<br/>يتأمل نصرالله في هذا المشروع 125 عاما من تاريخ الشعب الفل</span>
  <span id="freeText1304862412799914467" style="display:none">متزامنة مع الذكرى الستين لاحتلال فلسطين, تصدر (زمن الخيول البيضاء) رواية ملحمية استثنائية يتوج بها الشاعر والروائي إبراهيم نصرالله مشروعه الروائي الكبير ( الملهاة الفلسطينية ) الذي بدأ العمل عليه منذ عام 1985 , و الذي صدر منه ست روايات لكل رواية أجواؤها الخاصة بهاو شخوصها و بناؤها الفني و استقلالها عن الروايات الأخرى<br />يتأمل نصرالله في هذا المشروع 125 عاما من تاريخ الشعب الفلسطيني برؤية نقدية عميقة و مستويات فنية راقية , انطلاقا من تلك الحقيقة الراسخة التي عمل عليها دائما و التي تقول بأن إيماننا بالقضايا الكبيرة يحتم علينا إيجاد مستويات فنية عالية للتعبير عنها</span>

<div id="review_522110560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/522110560" />
    <a title="Marieke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1386971-marieke"><img alt="Marieke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306621880p2/1386971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/522110560?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marieke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marieke" href="/user/show/1386971-marieke">Marieke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789774164897" href="/book/show/13583271-time-of-white-horses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=islam">islam</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=mena-lit">mena-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=palestine-israel">palestine-israel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=arab-world">arab-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1386971-marieke?shelf=epic-like">epic-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer522110560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7943337948444146187">Wow. So...there is a genre we call creative non-fiction...non-fiction in a highly narrative form. Well, what about documentary fiction? Ibrahim Nasrallah has woven a novel out of actual events. Not just based on actual events, like many novels, but out of: he tells an epic story of one fictional Palestinian village, from the end of Ottoman Rule until 1948-ish when Zionism destroys the village and forces its inhabitants out. Throughout the novel Nasrallah includes italicized passages, which are t</span>
  <span id="freeText7943337948444146187" style="display:none">Wow. So...there is a genre we call creative non-fiction...non-fiction in a highly narrative form. Well, what about documentary fiction? Ibrahim Nasrallah has woven a novel out of actual events. Not just based on actual events, like many novels, but out of: he tells an epic story of one fictional Palestinian village, from the end of Ottoman Rule until 1948-ish when Zionism destroys the village and forces its inhabitants out. Throughout the novel Nasrallah includes italicized passages, which are the actual words of someone who experienced the events he has fictionalized. He also includes explanations in the form of footnotes, but rather than giving us bare facts, he allows himself to reflect on the facts, offering subjective commentary. As you can see, then, this is not an objective tale. It is highly subjective, telling the point(s) of view of the inhabitants of one village experiencing turbulent times. Yet it is done poetically, in short, connected vignettes. It took me months to get through it, but I enjoyed, as much as one can enjoy so much heartbreak, every moment I spent reading it. I did not read any of the original, but I did not feel like I was reading a translation. The translator deserves accolades, too. Truly masterful. I hope many in the English-speaking world will read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7943337948444146187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_829149828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/829149828" />
    <a title="Susan Abulhawa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24108689-susan-abulhawa"><img alt="Susan Abulhawa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596991915p2/24108689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/829149828?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan Abulhawa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan Abulhawa" href="/user/show/24108689-susan-abulhawa">Susan Abulhawa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer829149828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15510602039020932273">I wrote about this book in a longer piece: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.palestinechronicle.com/reading-time-of-white-horses-at-time-of-the-writer-in-durban/#.Ut03vP30C-o'>http://www.palestinechronicle.com/rea...</a><br/><br/>here are the relevant portions:<br/><br/>It’s safe to say that a book you can’t put down is a good one. But I’ve come across a novel I can’t recommend enough, even though it took me months to finish. TIME OF WHITE HORSES, by my friend, Ibrahim Nasrallah, was a fabulous read that I had to put down, repeatedly.<br/><br/>I read the first 300 pages of this translated work from the original Arabic in just a few days. Then the world change</span>
  <span id="freeText15510602039020932273" style="display:none">I wrote about this book in a longer piece: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.palestinechronicle.com/reading-time-of-white-horses-at-time-of-the-writer-in-durban/#.Ut03vP30C-o">http://www.palestinechronicle.com/rea...</a><br /><br />here are the relevant portions:<br /><br />It’s safe to say that a book you can’t put down is a good one. But I’ve come across a novel I can’t recommend enough, even though it took me months to finish. TIME OF WHITE HORSES, by my friend, Ibrahim Nasrallah, was a fabulous read that I had to put down, repeatedly.<br /><br />I read the first 300 pages of this translated work from the original Arabic in just a few days. Then the world changed and I moved through the next 300 pages slowly, tiptoeing through lives I recognised and characters I came to love. I turned these pages with trepidation for nearly a month, sometimes holding my breath and swallowing hard. I was reading the unfolding of my own life, and the lives of all Palestinians. I knew what was going to happen and in the strange ways of a heart touched by literature, I wanted to warn the characters. I needed them to make different decisions to save us all from our fate; until, I finally came upon the last chapter and stopped. I put the book down and left it there for another 2 weeks. Along with other reading material, I carried this thick hardback with me on a flight to South Africa. The final chapter was only 5 pages long, but I didn’t read them on the flight. In my hotel room in Johannesburg, I put the book on the table by my bed, looked at its it’s beautiful cover, an image painted by Nasrallah himself, and I read other books instead. I did the same thing a week later when I flew to Durban to take part in Time of the Writer literature festival.<br /><br />……<br /><br />Despite the assaults of fatigue, I picked up TIME OF WHITE HORSES and opened it to my bookmark. A few agonising minutes later, I had finished the final chapter. I closed the cover, put the book back on the bedside table, and wept. I had walked around carrying that final chapter for over 3 weeks, wanting but unable to look at it. I knew what was going to happen. I knew zionist thieves and thugs were going to take everything and rip all our hearts out one generation after another for the next six decades after the last chapter. I knew my grandmother and thousands of grandmothers were going to rot away as refugees in shacks until they died while European Jews occupied their homes. I knew our lives were going to fall and crumble and we would be blamed for our own miserable fate while a Zionist boot pressed on our necks. But I had hoped, for all those weeks, that the villagers of Hadiya would miraculously turn things around and stay and defeat those Zionist gangs and change the world.<br /><br />Alas, Palestine was stolen and we all died all over again in the last 5 pages. I fell asleep with the remains of that long day in Durban, the wreckage of that final chapter, and the lullaby of the Indian Ocean coming through my open waterfront hotel window. A few hours later, my body’s annoying habit of rising with the sun had me dragging my mind to the breakfast room in the lobby at 6am. I walked holding hands with the newly dispossessed villagers of Hadiya in TIME OF WHITE HORSES. The ineffable sorrow and humiliation of being carted away, as if cattle, from everything they knew and everything they were so that new Jewish arrivals could take their place, was part of that morning in a Durban hotel restaurant.<br /><br />……<br /><br />The theme of Time of the Writer literature festival was “writing a new world” and it turned out to be fitting that I carried a hardback of the past with me, even with only 5 pages to go. TIME OF WHITE HORSES is made of short chapters, each a sort of self-contained story of different characters in the village of Hadiya. The chapters are akin to individual pieces of a larger whole and as the reader moves from one to another, the pieces begin to fit together as if a puzzle, until a beautiful tortured nation emerges from the pages. What emerges, too, are patterns of human behaviour, including the “colonised mentality”. Given X, some people will do Y. Given imperial power, some subjects will collaborate. Given occupation and colonialism, most will resist. Some will want to negotiate and others will insist on a fight. Heroes emerged from the story of Hadiya and the downfall of the village, indeed of the country, could not have been accomplished without the cooperation of collaborators. The appeasers wanted to negotiate with the Ottomans or the British, and now zionists.<br /><br />In hindsight, the ones who clearly had it right were those who stood defiant, in full possession of themselves as an indigenous people, heirs to their own lands and their own heritage. They were the Andile Mngxitamas and Steve Bikos of their time and country. Had we but listened to them and followed their lead! Instead, we trudge in the molasses of a neo-liberal discourse of “nuance” trying to find our way through a maze of racist negotiations ands accords and settlements that are clearly wiping Palestine off the map. If I could write a new world, I would start it with the closing line in my friend Ibrahim Nasrallah’s novel TIME OF WHITE HORSES. It is a quote we all know well, by David Ben Gurion, who was born a Polish man named David Grunn. He said:<br /><br />“If I were an Arab leader I would never make terms with Israel. That is natural: we have taken their country…They only see one thing: we have come here and stolen their country. Why should they accept that?”<br /><br />Why, indeed?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15510602039020932273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3860640075325467235" style="display:none">Another great book by Ibrahim Nasrallah. This 509 pages novel needs from you time to finish it, it actually took me to get rid of my mobile for more than one day. Reading it is like going through a journey to Palestine before everything has started. It's a great book that shows what real men are, what real Palestinians are and what the land means to them. It shows how much they suffered to keep it while few helped them when every single person shouldv'e done that!.. I learned a lot from that great novel; about identity, love, family, loyality, the real meaning of what men and women are and a wonderful meaning of what Palestine is and for whom does it belong.<br />It also made me wonder whether Britain have ever given an official apologise of what it's done to Palestine.<br />One of the benefits of reading books is that they give you great knowledge of things and this book was definitely one of them. ♥</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2802520666?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/44188652-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2802520666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6493329190864422088">I’m so pleased this book was translated, and masterfully so, by Hoopoe Fiction.<br/><br/>The characters and stories will never leave me. Khalid the martyr, Hamama, and more. I’ve read quite a bit about Palestine, but the accounts of the evil acts by the British was largely new to me. <br/><br/>Arabic literature is about the art of storytelling. Time is taken. Prose is crafted. The author is an artist engaging in an art. Modern English literature is about getting a story told, usually in under 250 pages. Nasrallah i</span>
  <span id="freeText6493329190864422088" style="display:none">I’m so pleased this book was translated, and masterfully so, by Hoopoe Fiction.<br /><br />The characters and stories will never leave me. Khalid the martyr, Hamama, and more. I’ve read quite a bit about Palestine, but the accounts of the evil acts by the British was largely new to me. <br /><br />Arabic literature is about the art of storytelling. Time is taken. Prose is crafted. The author is an artist engaging in an art. Modern English literature is about getting a story told, usually in under 250 pages. Nasrallah is a brilliant writer and this book a masterpiece, but one I unfortunately think many American readers won’t appreciate sufficiently because of the stylistic differences. I loved it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6493329190864422088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1788864795" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788864795" />
    <a title="Reem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5493237-reem"><img alt="Reem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474287816p2/5493237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788864795?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reem" href="/user/show/5493237-reem">Reem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788864795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11022219249678369738">I'm intentionally writing this in English, so hopefully not only Arabs would visualize the impact of such a novel, the impact of the reality and the catastrophe this novel conveys. <br/>For me, a Palestinian Arab, who is the second generation of the people Zaman Al-Khuyoul Albaydaa' (the novel) tells their story, reading the book was not simple by any means. <br/>Some of the readers might wonder why am I making such a fuss out of a novel, since millions had been written over the course of time, well, let </span>
  <span id="freeText11022219249678369738" style="display:none">I'm intentionally writing this in English, so hopefully not only Arabs would visualize the impact of such a novel, the impact of the reality and the catastrophe this novel conveys. <br />For me, a Palestinian Arab, who is the second generation of the people Zaman Al-Khuyoul Albaydaa' (the novel) tells their story, reading the book was not simple by any means. <br />Some of the readers might wonder why am I making such a fuss out of a novel, since millions had been written over the course of time, well, let me just enlighten you that when you read a book that depicts the brutal way your ancestors has been slaughtered, hanged, beaten, raped out of their home, identity and being altogether, it shakes you to your core. Especially since the book that I read before this one depicts the diaspora that caused this diaspora. And it made me think. It made me question who I am. Who are the Arabs the we have long praised their sense of worth, generousity and dignity. It made me realize how the religions have been used as a commodity for some tycoons scattered around the world, to fill their greedy filthy souls. Because, sadly, the history is so obvious to everyone of us, and it is heart-wrenching, so literally it makes you feel a chest-ache, a kind that you have never experienced before. It is sad and terrifying how much a person with a bunch of dollars would do so he can keep these dollars, how he would trade his people solely to fulfill his lusty soul's needs. And petrifying to the same extent, how a group of people who have nothing in this world but themselves and their sense of worth, how much they would do, to save their homeland, their lives and their identity. And it is beautiful all the same. <br />The artistic way that the author masters in the novel is ultimately what the Palestinian catastrophe-nakbah has been thirsty for, for over 68 years. I have to admit that the 50 first pages were not quite enticing, but now I understand why the author had to make them that way, so he can introduce the grandiose Palestinian Comedy. The charachters are so well written that you wonder what their next move might be, and who would you like to be if you were one of them. <br />I am so grateful and thankful for Mr.Ibrahim Nasrallah for perfecting this masterpiece. The tremendous effort that has been put into this novel is appreciated by every soul that has owned and cherished this land. <br />There are no words to describe my gratitude, thank you Mr.Ibrahim. <br />P.S. I am not quite sure if I am writing a review or spilling my guts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11022219249678369738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_726460805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/726460805" />
    <a title="DubaiReader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2368681-dubaireader"><img alt="DubaiReader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262556200p2/2368681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/726460805?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DubaiReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DubaiReader" href="/user/show/2368681-dubaireader">DubaiReader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789774164897" href="/book/show/13583271-time-of-white-horses">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2368681-dubaireader?shelf=kutub-bk-grp">kutub-bk-grp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2368681-dubaireader?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer726460805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer298837348361395832">The Palestinian heritage.<br/><br/>This impressive work tells the fascinating story of the life of a village from the turn of the twentieth century until the incoming Jews of 1948 absorb the land and the villagers become refugees. Although fiction, the narrative is based on fact, interspersed with italicised quotes from people who survived those turbulent times. It is also an interesting mix of narrative and mythology.<br/><br/>We mainly follow the fortunes of a family living in the village of Hadiya (meaning Peace</span>
  <span id="freeText298837348361395832" style="display:none">The Palestinian heritage.<br /><br />This impressive work tells the fascinating story of the life of a village from the turn of the twentieth century until the incoming Jews of 1948 absorb the land and the villagers become refugees. Although fiction, the narrative is based on fact, interspersed with italicised quotes from people who survived those turbulent times. It is also an interesting mix of narrative and mythology.<br /><br />We mainly follow the fortunes of a family living in the village of Hadiya (meaning Peaceful), headed by Hajj Mahmud, and succeeded by his son Khalid. Khalid rescues a striking white mare, al-Hamama, which eventually becomes his and which he is totally obsessed by.<br />The life of such a village is poetically described, with many anecdotes of village life. Marriages, births, deaths, and the growing of crops, all take place at a leisurely pace, until life is turned upside down by the threat of war and defense of the land.<br /><br />My lowly rating of only three stars is based on my actual enjoyment of reading the book, which I found rather tedious and long-winded. However, writing this, three months after finishing the book, I realise that it has left a lasting impression on me, of how the Zionists infiltrated Palestinian lands, insidiously squeezing out the native Palestinians.<br /><br />The author, born to Palestinian parents in Jordan in 1954, grew up in a refugee camp there and is uniquely placed to narrate this story. The translation, by Nancy Roberts, was smooth and lucid. A difficult book to read but well worth the effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="298837348361395832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7228019718994458520" style="display:none">Probably the longest literature I have ever read since Orhan Pamuk. Despite the reading period that streches over than one year (I began in June 2016 and stopped for quite some time), the characters in the previous chapters remain fresh and sorrowful. Ibraham Nasrallah did a great job illustrating the gripping tragedy of the fall of Palestine from late Ottoman times to the establishment of the State of Israel in 1948. <br /><br />"If I was an Arab leader I would never make terms with Israel. That is natural: we have taken their country. Sure, God promised it to us, but what does that matter to them? There has been anti-Semitism, the Nazis, Hitler, Auschwitz, but was that their fault? They only see one thing: we have come here and stolen their country. Why would they accept that?" (David Ben Gurion, former President of the World Zionist Organisation) in the Jewish Paradox, 1978.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7VR2cxVqOWHyMlSS2WIxyIADcoRdvfmfPpQ7it4uwneVL2N4CPtZGuBfpog0osdaz2BoiS3Cm8VA+ax1lUnDWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2aTRetk3ibHglxyi82ymGO4ZmeW9zjWpR2UNphjxy3Gh38RxxKbpyvL67rgerFCKoXqD6M2xV/M5CJpZU5bKXw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10018045840718018540">Ibrahim Nasrallah is a Palestinian poet, novelist, professor, painter and photographer.<br/>He was born in the Wihdat Palestinian refugee camp in Jordan.<br/>He studied in UNRWA schools in the camp and got his teaching degree from a training college in the camp. He taught in Saudi Arabia for 2 years and worked as a journalist between 1978 and 1996. Nasrallah then returned to Jordan and worked at Dostur, Afa</span>
  <span id="freeText10018045840718018540" style="display:none">Ibrahim Nasrallah is a Palestinian poet, novelist, professor, painter and photographer.<br />He was born in the Wihdat Palestinian refugee camp in Jordan.<br />He studied in UNRWA schools in the camp and got his teaching degree from a training college in the camp. He taught in Saudi Arabia for 2 years and worked as a journalist between 1978 and 1996. Nasrallah then returned to Jordan and worked at Dostur, Afaq and Hasad newspapers. He is in charge of cultural activities at Darat-al-Funun in Amman. He has published 14 books of poetry, 13 novels and two children's books. . In 2009 his novel "The Time of White Horses" was shortlisted for the International Booker Prize for Arabic Fiction.<br />Nasrallah is a member of the Sakakini General Assembly. In 2006, Ibrahim Nasrallah decided to dedicate himself fully to his writing profession.<br /></span>
